B0040QYROK|5.0|Released in 1927, amid the golden age of the silent film era, Fritz Lang's METROPOLIS is a stylistic tour-de-force that has remained influential for the rest of the century, inspiring films from \\"Frankenstein\\" in 1931, \\"Bladerunner\\" in 1982, to \\"Dark City\\" in 1997. With its imaginative set design, elaborate photography, bold editing, and its then groundbreaking special effects, this German sci-fi silent classic exemplifies the highly inventive period of German Expressionism, which also include such film masterworks as \\"The Cabinet of Dr. Caligaru\\", \\"Nosferatu\\", \\"The Last Laugh\\", and Lang's \\"Die Nibelungen\\".<br /><br />The 2010 Kino Region-A Blu-ray edition (and its corresponding Region-1 DVD edition) is titled \\"The Complete Metropolis\\" to avoid confusion with earlier DVD editions. It contains, to date, the most complete, two-and-a-half-hour cut of the film, combining the two-hour version from the monumental 2001 restoration effort by Germany's F.W. Murnau Foundation (previously released as the 2003 Kino DVD), and about half-hour of footage discovered at Museo del Cine in Buenos Aires, Argentina in 2008 that had been unseen for decades. This previously lost footage has been edited back into the film to create this new \\"Complete Metropolis\\" edition. The added scenes are sprinkled all over the film, improving continuity, clarifying storytelling, and thus heightening the impact and yielding a result that is greater than the sum of its parts, as they finally restore Lang's full vision to its near complete form.<br /><br />The HD picture quality of the Blu-ray ranges from sparklingly clear in some footage, slightly softer in others (especially the special fx shots), to severely battered and damaged as in those newly-discovered shots. All the \\"good-looking\\" footage came from the 2001 restoration. With the upgrade to HD, the sharpness and the clarity over the DVD counterpart is readily apparent, and therefore this Blu-ray represents the best that the film has ever looked onhome video. Unfortunately, the half hour of new-found footage, originated from 16mm film, looks severely damaged and sometimes barely watchable, and it doesn't benefit much from the HD picture. As the new footage is sprinkled all over the film, the picture quality oscillates between good and bad, normally an uncomfortable experience but a small price to pay for finally watching the most complete version yet of the classic.<br /><br />The Blu-ray disc contains a lossless DTS 5.1 audio track of the original orchestral score by Gottfried Huppertz, performed by Berlin's Rundfunk Symphony Orchestra. Many viewers, like myself, were disappointed that Alloy Orchestra's own uniquely interpretative score was not included.  I contacted Alloy Orchestra and they said the German distributors would not allow Kino to use their score on the new edition. Thus, Alloy Orchestra is selling their score on a CD disc, albeit in lossy MP3 format with only a 192 kbps bit rate. Google \\"alloy metropolis order\\" to order it.<br /><br />The intertitles for the 2010 Kino edition, just like in the 2003 edition, are in English only. Whenever there is on-screen German text, English subtitles are provided and not removable.  If you are a stickler and prefer to see original German intertitles, just as the viewers saw it in 1927 Germany, you have to buy the British Region-B Blu-ray edition released by Eureka, titled \\"Metropolis\\", in which intertitles are in German only and supported by removable English subtitles.<br /><br />Supplements on Kino's 2010 edition do not contain any from the 2003 edition (so save that disc). Instead, we have a pretty good 50-minute documentary titled \\"Voyage to Metropolis\\", shown in HD on the Blu-ray and narrated in German with optional English subtitles, about the dramatic history of \\"Metropolis\\" up to its re-discovery in Argentina. (The same documentary is also on the Region-B disc. TCM has also broadcast another 50-min documentary on the same subject titled \\"Metropolis Refound\\", which is equally excellent but is not on home video.)<br /><br />(I mentioned the Region-B Blu-ray earlier so I might as well do a comparison with the Kino edition. The HD picture quality is virtually identical on the Kino edition and the Eureka \\"Master of Cinema\\" edition from Britain. Both have the same Rundfunk Symphony Orchestra score in lossless DTS. Both have the \\"Voyage to Metropolis\\" documentary (shown in HD on Blu-ray). The Eureka disc also contains an excellent full-length audio commentary by David Kalat and Jonathan Rosenbaum, while the Kino disc has a 9-minute interview with Paula Felix-Didier, curator of the Museo del Cine in Buenos Aires. The Eureka disc also comes with a 56-page booklet of essays, interviews, and restoration notes. So in terms of supplements, the Eureka edition seems a better offer -- to those who can play Region-B discs.)

B0068RHGJM|4.0|Anyone who knows me knows I am a huge Nightwish fan.  I discovered them with Oceanborn when I was in middle school, and have been obsessively buying their albums ever since.  I eagerly awaited Imaginaerum, though with a bit of trepidation -- what if I didn't like it?  I'm happy to say that this is not the case.<br /><br />Imaginaerum is a very bold, over-the-top album -- very Nightwish, pretty much.  It does have some flaws, however.  I think the best way for me to write this is to go through it song by song, though I will try to keep it as succinct as possible (I failed.  After the list I have a few general items about the album if you just want those).<br /><br />1. Taikatalvi - 3.5/5 - I'm not a huge fan of slower songs, and Nightwish's in particular tend to leave me wanting more.  I agree with another reviewer who says that this song doesn't really fit in with the rest of the album.  It reminds me of a creepy lullaby, though, which IS pretty fitting as an intro.  But it's not a song I can listen to every time it comes up in my playlist.<br /><br />2. Storytime - 4.5/5 - This song grew on me.  When I first listened to it I was a bit thrown off, but it didn't take long for me to be impressed by Annette's singing, the lyrics, and the fast-paced music.  The song is very captivating and helps to further drive the story introduced by Taikatalvi.  I only took 1/2 a star off because it DID take a few listens before it really grew on me.<br /><br />3. Ghost River - 5/5 - I don't know what it says about me that I immediately latched onto this song and listened to it constantly.  It's a relatively heavy song with vocals from both Annette and Marko, and it came out very awesome -- the child's choir adds an excellent creepy aspect to it, and the music just sounds amazing.  This, I think, is the kind of music I expect from Nightwish -- bombastic.<br /><br />4. Slow Love Slow - 4/5 - This is another song that had to grow on me, though I still can't listen to it every time it shows up.  This is a random Jazz beat, which honestly doesn't really flow well after Ghost River, and while Annette sounds fantastic in it, it is NOT what I associate with Nightwish at all.  I would have liked if they tried to turn it into a jazz metal song -- this is Nightwish, I expect them to do crazy things like that.  So overall, it is a beautiful song, but a bit too slow and unexpected, especially at first.<br /><br />5. I Want my Tears Back - 4/5 - A Nightwish folk metal song.  There are strong folk influences throughout this song and the instrumentals are fantastic, while both Annette and Marko sound great.  My main problem is with the lyrics; at first I heard them and I just couldn't associate them with Nightwish.  But it grew on me pretty fast; I can't resist folk metal of this quality.  It flows surprisingly well from \\"Slow Love Slow\\".<br /><br />6. Scaretale - 4/5 - Around this time I start to think Nightwish is on drugs.  So I think this song is supposed to be creepy and haunting, especially considering the lyrics and Annette's impressive performance (how does she sing like that?).  However... I just find it hilarious.  No offense meant to Nightwish at ALL, as the song is extremely well-done and has great atmosphere.  I just can't imagine Marko as a crazy circus dude.  This song is somewhat heavy with some great imagery, with that circus feeling being most present in this song.<br /><br />7. Arabesque - 4.5/5 - This instrumental comes rather abruptly after \\"Scaretale\\", but is very atmospheric of some Arabian desert, and sounds great.  I don't have too much to say about it since it's a bit short except that I do enjoy it, I just wish it was a bit longer and perhaps had more a Nightwish-type sound.<br /><br />8. Turn Loose the Mermaids - 3.5/5 - Another song that had to grow on me, this is a pretty ballade with some pretty fascinating lyrics (\\"I checked your teeth and warmed your toes\\"?) with I think someone said Celtic influences?  It reminds me of \\"The Islander\\" from Dark Passion Play now that I think about it.  Again, though, I'm not a huge fan of Nightwish's slower songs, and so while I do think it's nice, it's not something I can listen to all day long.<br /><br />9. Rest Calm - 4/5 - I don't even know what rating to give this song because, uh, it just seems like a NIghtwish song to me.  Nothing about it stands out too strongly, though if I recall correctly this is the song that I was not expecting to be as heavy as it is (which isn't much, granted?).  I think the ending of the song is quite lovely; I thought the repetition worked out, and I enjoy the lyrics.<br /><br />10. The Crow, The Owl, and The Dove - 4/5 - This one is slowly growing on me.  I enjoy the lyrics and the music fits them quite well, but it's another slower song, and I feel like this album has too many slow songs, especially for Nightwish.  Edit - I'm not sure why I call this a slower song?  It's more like soft rock, but certainly not like \\"Slow Love Slow\\", for instance.  Just thought I'd clarify -- there definitely drums and guitars in this song, and it's very pretty overall.<br /><br />11. Last Ride of the Day - 5/5 - Why do I love this song so much?  I don't know.  I think it's because it's very traditional Nightwish -- bombastic music, soaring lyrics, interesting lyrics, overall just awesome.  More like \\"Dark Passion Play\\" than the rest of the album, to be sure.<br /><br />12. Song of Myself - 3/5 - Okay, I'm sorry.  But this song?  The first half is awesome.  It sounds similar to the last track, being airy, soaring... And then turns into spoken poetry.  I don't mind the first minute or two of it.  But then the guy says \\"Stop saying 'I know how you feel'.  How could anyone know how another feels.\\"  I'm sorry but that sounds like it came straight out of Tumblr and from then on I found the poetry mostly boring.  Also the children in the poetry section REALLY grate on my nerves; they sound like nails on a chalkboard.  And the lyrics overall are a bit too melodramatic for my tastes, ESPECIALLY when spoken as opposed to placed with music.  I can listen to it once in a while, but I often just skip the spoken part.<br /><br />13. Imaginaerum - 4/5 - This is okay.  I like how it takes elements from the entire album and puts into one soaring conclusion.  It doesn't really catch my interest often, though, even though musically it's pretty decent.<br /><br />Now for a few things I noted as I listened to this for six hours straight (In the car, it was a long drive)<br /><br />a) I LOVE the many unique things Annette is able to do with her voice -- she sounds haunted and insane in \\"Scaretale\\", sweet if a bit melancholy in \\"Turn Loose the Mermaids\\", and powerful in \\"Last Ride of the Day\\".  Annette's singing definitely helped make the album as solid as it is.  Marko also did an excellent job -- his voice has finally grown on me, and he was great in \\"Ghost River\\" in particular.<br /><br />b) Where is the metal?  I missed the band in a lot of the songs -- \\"Slow Love Slow\\", \\"Turn Loose the Mermaids\\", \\"Imaginaerum\\"... I almost felt like this album was more \\"orchestra with a back-up metal band\\" than \\"metal band with an orchestra\\".  Songs like \\"Ghost River\\", \\"Last Ride of the Day\\", \\"Storytime\\", and \\"I Want My Tears Back\\" at least convinced me they were SOMEWHERE, but having six out of thirteen songs be ballades or \\"slow\\" really threw me off.<br /><br />So onto what you guys want to know.... Will YOU like this album?<br /><br />For Old Nightwish Lovers -- Be patient with it.  It IS different from their original stuff, but there are some worthy songs on the album.  Is it their best album?  I don't think so (I don't know what is).  Is it better than, say, Oceanborn?  Probably not (I'd rate them about even).  But I DID enjoy it, and I do think it is worth buying.<br /><br />If you like the band mostly, note what I said above: about half of the album is more orchestral than metal, in my opinion.  It's still very pretty, but asa metal addict, it threw me off.<br /><br />So overall?  I think the album came together pretty well, with some gorgeous musical genius and only one or two songs that I honestly can say I did not like that much.  I then rate this as an average Nightwish album for me, and thus I'm sure it will appear in my playlist for years to come.  If you like Nightwish's unique sound and would like to see what crazy things they've thought up next, I recommend you pick this album up.  Just be sure to give it an open mind.<br /><br />Thank you for reading my review, and happy listening!<br /><br />(PS. If there are any obvious grammatical/spelling errors, please let me know!  My meds make me mix up words in rather hilarious ways, but I'd rather not confuse anyone.)e, but I often just skip the spoken part.  13. Imaginaerum - 4/5 - This is okay.  I like how it takes elements from the entire album and puts into one soaring conclusion.  It doesn't really catch my interest often, though, even though musically it's pretty decent.  Now for a few things I noted as I listened to this for six hours straight (In the car, it was a long drive)  a) I LOVE the many unique things Annette is able to do with her voice -- she sounds haunted and insane in \\"Scaretale\\", sweet if a bit melancholy in \\"Turn Loose the Mermaids\\", and powerful in \\"Last Ride of the Day\\". 0439023513|3.0|With this series meeting its end I find myself at a bit of a crossroads. The tragedy that strikes in Mockingjay is so immense, so heartbreaking, and deep rooted that it required me to step back at moments and just breath. By no means would I expect or require a false portrayal of this story's end. I don't want to feel lied to anymore than Katniss does, but it was arguably the hardest book in the series to get through.<br /><br />The plot is thick and entrapping, not letting you go until the very end and even then, it still holds you hostage. The characters that we've grown attached to have come to suffer in some of the worst ways imaginable and for some, the fight will never be over. This story is sad yet eerily on point with what could very well be a scary reality. It isn't sugar coated or censored to save its audience heart-ship. This book is a testament to pain, suffering, and the cost of freedom.<br /><br />As far as characters go, I found it very saddening to watch Katniss lose herself and all that she loved to The Game. A game it seemed she could never fully escape. I watched helplessly as she suffered and fought against herself and others to find hope or love or anything worth holding onto. I've read in some review that she is viewed as a selfish girl without love in her heart. That she is weak or that she is cold and unlovable. I see Katniss and I can't help but disagree. Did she love him? Yes, of course, in some way. But no matter how this story ended I see Katniss as a woman stripped of the ability to choose and love wholly. She must survive and that is all she knows how to do anymore.<br /><br />It's a sad story with a satisfying ending all things considered but I would argue that Katniss never made any choices in life but to stay alive. This story isn't about love, it's about survival. B006QVRVJK|2.0|I have a lot of catching up to do when it comes to Roman Polanski films. Rosemary's Baby, Chinatown, and The Pianist are all patiently biding their time in my Netflix queue waiting on me to get around to them and watch them for the first time. The Polanski films I have seen had the potential to be great, but kind of let everything they had going for it slip through the cracks as the film went on. I remember being fascinated by The Ninth Gate, but was extremely disappointed once the ending rolled around. There was also quite a bit of praise being thrown around for The Ghost Writer last year and it just didn't affect me the way any of that praise did for other critics. So while Carnage has gotten many accolades as one of the funniest movies of last year, I took it with a grain of salt. People seem to generally love Polanski and that's fine. His films are genuinely a pleasure to look at as the cinematography is always fantastic, but it certainly seems as though he may not be as great as everyone makes him out to be.<br /><br />Carnage is basically a 74-minute discussion between two couples whose eleven and twelve year old sons got into a fight. Penelope (Jodie Foster) and Michael Longstreet's (John C. Reilly) son Ethan was struck in the face with a stick by Zachary, the son of Nancy (Kate Winslet) and Alan Cowan (Christoph Waltz). The parents get together to try and find a way for Zachary and Ethan to talk things out, but everything eventually falls apart and the two couples are eventually at each other's throats.<br /><br />This was not the hilarious movie it was made out to be. While the other people in the theater seemed to be howling at everything on screen, it mostly just felt slightly snicker worthy at times. John C. Reilly is pretty funny. His views, the things that come out of his mouth, his character, and his performance are probably the closest thing to hilarious Carnage has to offer. \\"Is cobbler cake or pie?\\", the flush mechanisms conversation, \\"You certainly perked up after...\\", the hamster story, the doodle nickname being ridiculous, and \\"YOU'RE BLOWING THIS OUT OF PROPORTION!\\" are all mostly entertaining thanks to John C. Reilly's over the top performance. Michael Longstreet is probably the closest you'll come to relating to one of the on-screen characters, as well. The film is mostly a competition between four egomaniacal individuals competing for the spotlight though. Christoph Waltz's \\"god of carnage\\" speech is pretty amazing as is the \\"disfigured his schoolmate\\" conversation, but you want to slap the hell out of Alan Cowan the minute you realize he cherishes his phone more than anything else in the world. Kate Winslet is mostly nauseous and drunk the entire film and you probably won't walk away from this without thinking of Jodie Foster's bulbous, veiny, pulsating neck. Seriously, that thing will probably haunt your dreams the night after seeing this.<br /><br />Carnage is very short. It feels like it ends as soon as it begins. It's like Cloverfield length. It also has one of the worst endings ever. How many films can you name that stop with a phone call? Nothing is resolved. Everything just stops. Despite a wonderful cast and a few chuckle worthy moments, Carnage mostly falls flat. It comes off as more of a contest between two married couples that become more interested in pointing out the flaws of their marriage rather than the task at hand. Maybe it's because I work in retail and I witness these kinds of conversations on a daily basis, but it just wasn't very entertaining at all. Carnage stumbles on the thin line between being extremely annoying and being mildly amusing.\\", the hamster story, the doodle nickname being ridiculous, and \\"YOU'RE BLOWING THIS OUT OF PROPORTION!\\" are all mostly entertaining thanks to John C. Reilly's over the top performance. Michael Longstreet is probably the closest you'll come to relating to one of the on-screen characters, as well. The film is mostly a competition between four egomaniacal individuals competing for the spotlight though. Christoph Waltz's \\"god of carnage\\" speech is pretty amazing as is the \\"disfigured his schoolmate\\" conversation, but you want to slap the hell out of Alan Cowan the minute you realize he cherishes his phone more than anything else in the world. Kate Winslet is mostly nauseous and drunk the entire film and you probably won't walk away from this without thinking of Jodie Foster's bulbous, veiny, pulsating neck. Seriously, that thing will probably haunt your dreams the night after seeing this.  Carnage is very short. It feels like it ends as soon as it begins. It's like Cloverfield length. It also has one of the worst endings ever. How many films can you name that stop with a phone call? Nothing is resolved. Everything just stops. Despite a wonderful cast and a few chuckle worthy moments, Carnage mostly falls flat. It comes off as more of a contest between two married couples that become more interested in pointing out the flaws of their marriage rather than the task at hand. Maybe it's because I work in retail and I witness these kinds of conversations on a daily basis, but it just wasn't very entertaining at all. Carnage stumbles on the thin line between being extremely annoying and being mildly amusing.

145162445X|4.0|A UNIVERSE FROM NOTHING BY LAWRENCE M. KRAUSS  A Review by Tim Campbell  Something from nothing!  The title alone will give the hard core fundamentalists conniptions and will confuse most other religionists.  But the universe according to Dr. Krauss does not require a magic being in order to exist and the \\"nothing\\" of which Dr. Krauss writes is anything but nothing.  In fact, \\"nothing\\" refers to the vacuum of empty space, which, rather than being an empty nothingness is actually teeming with energies and particles and stuff, all of which contribute to our universe, and us, being what and how we are!  Dr. Lawrence M. Krauss is a well-known and highly respected theoretical physicist and cosmologist. He is Foundations Professor and Director of the Origins Project at Arizona State University.  He is author or co-author of more than three hundred scientific publications and eight books including a best seller: THE PHYSICS OF STAR TREK.  And yes, to be forthcoming here in this review, Dr. Krauss and I are both unbelievers in tribal gods, including Yahweh, the god of the Hebrew Bible and alleged father of Jesus.  As Dr. Krauss has argued before and explains most eloquently here, \\"Forget Jesus. The stars died so you could be born.  A UNIVERSE FROM NOTHING does not answer definitively the question of how the universe originated.  The book offers the best and most plausible natural explanations for the existence of something rather than nothing, and Dr. Krauss explains in fairly easy-to-understand terms how science has arrived at it conclusions and what enormous pillars of evidence support the likelihood of its conclusions.  Gravity, Gravitational lensing, Type 1a Supernovas, Clustering of Galaxies, Inflationary Theory, General Relativity, Einstein's Cosmological Constant, Hubble's Constant (which ironically changes over cosmic time due to the effects of Gravity), the age of the Universe to four digits (13.72 billion years), the certainty of the Big Bang (supported by three pillars of observed and predicted evidence:  the Hubble expansion of the Universe, the Cosmic Microwave Background Radiation with a current measure temperature exactly as predicted by BB Theory, and the almost exact agreement between the predicted abundance of light elements and the observed and precisely measured abundance of these elements: hydrogen, Helium, Deuterium, and Lithium) are all covered and explained.    As a side note, Dr. Krauss points out that these \\"light\\" elements are the only elements that could have been produced in the course of the Big Bang and the subsequent expansion and cooling of the Universe.  ALL of the heavier elements--carbon, oxygen, nitrogen, iron, and so on, in other words the things that make US--could only have been produced later by the atomic effects of exploding stars. These are the Supernovas, the result of giant stars burning through their hydrogen fuel and dying in a cataclysmic explosion of radiation and newly formed heavy elements.  As he puts it somewhat poetically, our own Milky Way Galaxy has seen more than two hundred million of these supernovas since forming billions of years ago.  The matter formed by these explosions became the matter that then formed our planet and then us.  The atoms in your left hand most certainly came from a different star than the atoms in your right hand.  We are all stardust!  These ideas and topics and much more are discussed and explained throughout the book.  Dr. Krauss does an excellent job of making these powerful  and complex concepts accessible to the layman.  While a background in science would certainly be helpful, the average person can still read this book and be both entertained as well as educated.  Dr. Krauss is one of a number of renowned scientists who have taken time away from their own work in order to bring their work to the rest of us.  Along with Neil deGrasse Tyson, Evalyn Gates, Richard Dawkins, Jerry Coyne, and others, Dr. Krauss is following in the tradition of Carl Sagan and Isaac Asimov as an \\"explainer of science\\".    The book is written in a clear and concise manner and not laden down with difficult-to-understand math or jargon that would be understandable only to another physicist.    The future of the Universe is also examined.  Not the silly theological predictions for May, 2012, or any of the infamous Harold Camping oopses, but rather the eventual fate of a Universe in which normal matter and energy (Us) comprise only about 4% of the actual stuff of the Universe with a whopping 70% being comprised of an unknown, but pretty darn certain stuff that physicists amusingly call Dark Energy.  And it is this DE that makes it possible for us to get \\"something\\" from \\"nothing\\".  This is the energy of empty space, the force that fills the vacuum and pushed the universe (space itself) to expand and to expand at an even faster rate, so that one day, in about two trillion years, whoever may be around at that time, will not know what the universe actually is!  As Dr. Krauss puts it, \\"We live at a very special time...the only time when we can observationally verify that we live at a very special time\\".  Another poignant side note:  the late Christopher Hitchens was supposed to write a forward for this book, but his health had deteriorated to the point where he was unable to complete the commitment.  Biologist and also best-selling author Richard Dawkins stepped in and wrote an afterword.    Writes Dawkins (referring to the theologians' arguments of design): \\"And now we can read Lawrence Krauss for what looks to me like the knockout blow. Even the last remaining trump card of the theologian, `why is there something rather than nothing?' shrivels up before your eyes as you read these pages. If ON THE ORIGIN OF SPECIES was biology's deadliest blow to supernaturalism, we may come to see A UNIVERSE FROM NOTHING as the equivalent from cosmology. The title means exactly what it says. And what it says is devastating.\\"  Eloquent, entertaining, funny, and ironic, A UNIVERSE FROM NOTHING represents the triumph of reason and evidence-based science over irrational and revelatory-based superstition.

B0000DD7LB|5.0|A KID'S REVIEW:  2002 was a year of worldwide success and acclaim for Britney but it also had its bad moments for her (for example: breaking up with her boyfriend Justin Timberlake), and after her Dream Within A Dream Tour in support of her third album 'Britney' ended in July 2002, she announced she would take a break from her career for half a year. Britney had written new songs while touring that year for her next album but didn't know what the new album's direction was, so she decided to take the break. In November 2002, she started going to the studio to record some of the written songs for the album and knew the album's direction: Lots of dancing, with touches of empowerment and mature themes. The songs that came out in the first sessions were 'Touch Of My Hand' and 'Everytime' (this one being a response to Justin Timberlake's 'Cry Me A River', both talk about their breakup). Sessions continued throughout 2003, and in May 2003 she previewed some finished songs to MTV including 'Touch Of My Hand', 'Everytime' and 'Brave New Girl'. In September 2003, she made the first live performance of one of the album's songs 'Me Against The Music' and promotion for the album started. She continued to make live performances of the album's songs and eventually released 'Me Against The Music' as the album's first single in October 2003, which was a duet with Madonna. The album was released in November 2003, and I'll review the songs now and give a conclusion:  1. Me Against The Music - The album's first track and first single. This is a duet with the queen of pop Madonna, and both did it very well. The song is awesome, and its video is awesome as well, excellent choice for the first single since it totally fits the album theme about getting in the zone and letting go on the dance floor. I give it a 10/10  2. (I Got That) Boom Boom - The album's second track. This song features Ying Yang Twins, and they do it amazingly together with Britney. This song is urban, and for me it's one of the best on the album. I give it a 10/10  3. Showdown - The album's third track. I think this song together with 'Boom Boom' makes a tie because both are great and my favorite songs on the album. This song just has great vocals and great beats, and it's perfect. I give it a 10/10  4. Breathe On Me - The album's fourth track. The beat is great, but maybe I have listened to it too many times so it's not as great as the first listen (it was like the best song in the world when I first heard it). I give it 9/10  5. Early Mornin' - The album's fifth track. Very good song about messing at night and then it's suddenly morning, it's kinda hard to explain it, it's just pretty good. I give it a 9.5/10  6. Toxic - The album's sixth track and second single. This one is obviously a classic, Britney has named it as her favorite song of her entire career, and she's right, this also ties with 'Showdown' and 'Boom Boom'. She had to fight with her label for it to be released, because they wanted 'Boom Boom' as the second single, but since both are my faves I would have been happy with either. I give it a 10/10  7. Outrageous - The album's seventh track and fourth and final single. This is the only song I hate, it's just repeatitive and it's boring, and that's sad because the whole album is a masterpiece. I see this a filler and a terrible choice as a single, and to make it even worse, this song ruined Britney's career because when she was filming its video she injured her knee and that made her cancel the remainder of 2004's The Onyx Hotel Tour in support of 'In The Zone' (which was one of the best tours ever!) and affected her dancing forever. This song SUCKS, and I'm not ashamed to admit it, this should have never made it onto the final cut. I give it a 0/10  8. Touch Of My Hand - The album's eighth track. I really like this one, despite the lyrics and meaning, I really like its eastern, Oriental sound and this could have been a MUCH better choice as the fourth single ratherthan 'Outrageous', I just imagine her with a Chinese or Japanese outfit like a kimono and dancing to the song. I give it a 10/10  9. The Hook Up - The album's ninth track. Catchy song, catchy beat, not much to say about it. I give it a 9.5/10  10. Shadow - The album's tenth track. This is a ballad, and its lyrics are cute, but it's not her best or most powerful ballad, but it's still very good. I give it a 9.5/10  11. Brave New Girl - The album's eleventh track. I find funny how this kind of song is included on this album, considering she's heading in a more mature and serious direction and image, instead of touching themes about 'girls' like she did on the previous album, she's supposed to be a woman right? But I understand it, this was one of the first songs to be written and recorded for the album and of course she still didn't know the album's direction, and the song is actually great, her voice sounds funny and overall it's not bad at all (a masterpiece and even a good single choice compared to that 'Outrageous' trash). I give it an 8.5/10  12. Everytime - The album's twelfth track and third single. This is another ballad, but this one is one of her best and most powerful and talks about her breakup with Justin, responding to his song 'Cry Me A River'. This song is just really heartfelt and her vocals sound like fragile and show how she was really affected by the breakupthis is MUCH better than the cheesy 'I'm Not A Girl, Not Yet A Woman' from her previous album, but it's obvious since she wrote this with her friend Annet Artani and she doesn't write cheesy songs (except for 'Dear Diary' from the Oops! album, but it's understandable since it was one of her first attempts at songwriting). Overall, this is a masterpiece as well and a great choice as a single since it's the highlight ballad. I give it a 10/10  13. Me Against The Music (Rishi Rich's Desi Kulcha Remix) - The album's thirteenth and final track. A remix of the original song, this is an amazing remix and the best of this song, it's just as awesome as the original is. I give it a 10/10  My conclusion: This is Britney's best album to date, and I think it's very underrated (I can't believe how people say 'Blackout' is her best album when that album was just ok but nothing very special, way overrated album). The only bad thing about this album is that 'Outrageous' song mistake, it sucked and ruined Britney's career permanently since she's just not able to dance like before (she does great dance moves, but she's lost confidence because she's afraid of messing up and having another accident so she just makes simple moves), but ignoring that song this album is a masterpiece and doesn't have any filler, it's just too sad the era had to be cut because of the injury and all the promotion ended in June 2004, because this album had the potential to make awesome hits that would mark Britney's career (at least it made 1, I'm talking about 'Toxic'), but anyways... this album is a masterpiece and Britney's best album to date, and Britney wrote/co-wrote almost all of the album's songs and even was one of the producers, so obviously she's connected to it and it's more herself. Buy this album, you won't be disappointed (except for that annoying and stupid song I've been talking about).

B00006AW2M|4.0|I'll admit that I prioritized the purchase of this Stones' remaster much lower than stronger efforts from their 60's catalog but I am so glad I finally picked this up. Overall, the sonic upgrade is fantastic over my CD copy from 1990 & if you're nut for the killer bands (Stones, Beatles, Pink Floyd, etc.), you want the best sounding recordings in your collection.  Sure, this is not 12x5, Aftermath, Beggar's Banquet, or the monumental Let it Bleed - but it is a must-have in my opinion. Nowhere else have the Stones dared to be this strange and footloose. I also admittedly have a very soft spot for this LP, having grown up with it (& its original 3D cover) in the late 70s. It was holy grail, mystery of rock and roll, black magic kinda stuff to me as a kid. I recall entranced listens to it & occasionally it can reach that effect still - many dozens of listens later. It may or may not \\"deserve\\" it, but in my love of 60s pop-rock, I put this right up there with Magical Mystery Tour, Axis: Bold as Love, Freak Out!, Pet Sounds & SMiLE, Mr. Fantasy, Notorious Byrd Brothers, Disraeli Gears, Anthem of the Sun, and others cut from the same psychedelic cloth. It's simply a fun, cool album... from an era of fun, cool albums. I think some fans need to give it a break and enjoy it for what it is.  Now on with the DSD remaster...  Sing this song all together: A \\"welcome to our trip\\" kick-off, much like with The Beatles' \\"Magical Mystery Tour\\". The separation of the tracks is greatly improved over the old CD release. The stereo imaging of the group vocals is excellent (is that Lennon in the mix?) & the percussion in the middle instrumental is groovy.  Citadel is one of the few Stones recordings of 67 where you can really bridge the mid-60s contemporary art-rock to the power of their renewed return to their roots rock n' roll later in 68. To be fair, there was no Jimmy Miller directing production efforts at these sessions. Citadel retains the Stones' riff-based sound, thanks to Keith's creative hook. This song really stands out on the DSD remaster. Charlie's kit really explodes, the layers of overdubs & early synth reach out in the mix better, Mick's vocal is less muddled.  In Another Land is just a fun listen. I can't tell if they want the listener to take them seriously on this one or not. Regardless, holy %#$, it's cool to listen to. Amazing recording techniques & effect for its time. The Moog \\"wind\\" behind Wyman's vocal captures the imagination. Too bad the lyrics are just so damn campy.  2000 Man is a sleeper on this LP. I absolutely love the track. Funky drum track, awesome lyrics, backwards tracks, and a totally rockin' chorus. A Stones classic. Like Citadel, this one is a gem and really reaches out toward where the Stones were inevitably going with Beggar's Banquet. 2000 Man sounds great on vinyl, the old CD mix, and here as well. What you may notice is more dynamics between the verse and chorus.  Sing this all together (see what happens) is definitely not a focused effort by the future Glimmer Twins. Anything that starts off with Brian Jones asthmatic hacking cough isn't destined for greatness. Keith's layered parts are anything but inspired. The middle riff that kicks off the brass is a cool touch. There are a few other funky 4 bar \\"chunks\\" of music infused in this otherwise tripped-out mess. But really, this is just too much acid for anyone not on acid to really dig it. I'd assume they included it on the LP as a treat for those listeners who were as utterly wasted as they liked to get. The \\"aliens have landed\\" (and are saying, Merry Christmas?!?!) bit at the end of the first side kind of redeems 'See What Happens'. It's freaky and I like it.  She's a Rainbow is a beautiful piece of psychedelic pop. Sure, it's kind of the Stones' Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds - but I'm completely cool with that. The remaster sounds a bit cleaner. Nicky Hopkins & John Paul Jones' efforts really put the shine on this one. I can't believe I'm saying thisabout a Stones track, but the string arrangement really is tasteful. Rainbow is a cornerstone for the LP & was the right choice in kicking off the second side. Even with all the trippy flavor on this one, it's Charlie's playing that seals the track as a Stones work of art.  The Lantern is another under-rated Stones nugget. It's right up there with Dandelion and Have You Seen Your Mother, Baby?. The track certainly benefits from the newest remastering technology. The tape hiss is greatly reduced & the vocal harmonies are great. A close listen discloses (you can hear the bleed) that they decided to drop Keith's riffing through the first minute or so of the track - I suppose for dynamic effect. It's not super catchy but the bass/lead guitar interplay, drum fills, and sparse orchestral touches really make this song consistently enjoyable.  Gomper. The one song on the LP that's grown on me over 30 years. The song has pop structure but is bold in its experimental daring. When it's time to freak out, they go for it. My only complaint is that the hand drumming doesn't build enough to push the track through the madness.  2000 Light Years... is the strongest song on the album & one of the best Stones songs of their 60s catalog. The band's really grooving, Mick's vocals are amazing, and the synth effects remain cool and much less dated than many other recordings of the time. Play this one loud. A great match with the Floyd's Astronomy Domine on any mix/playlist.  On with the show - I've just never cared for this one but in the context of the record, I guess I get it. It's in line with Buttons & Something Happened... on a good note, the remaster of this does sound good. I'd much rather have had them include We Love You and pinch this one though. Let the LP end with 2000 Light Years From Home. That's just another Stones-head's opinion though.  Even if this can't touch Let it Bleed, Sticky Fingers, and Exile - it's worthy of inclusion in your Stones and/or 60's collection. Lightsome candles, embrace your inner freak, and enjoy the Rolling Stones like they only sounded in 1967. Oh mummy, proud of your sun!

B006DQ1J0K|5.0|Sony has recently been releasing Met broadcasts with a sticker that falsely proclaims \\"first time on CD.\\" While they might mean something like \\"first authorized time on CD\\", that's not what they say giving collectors the false impression that they're getting something that truly hasn't been available. This release of the 1 Dec 1962 broadcast has been available in the past but no longer. If you have the release on Movimento Musica, there's no reason to get this one. In all the ones I've compared (Sony to previous releases), the sound on the Sony release is identical to previous releases and the Sony CD contain no extra material such as announcements by Milton Cross or Peter Allen. If you want to find whether a broadcast has been released on CD, look it up Frank Hamilton's excellent website \\"[...]\\" and click on \\"Metropolitan Opera performances on CD\\".<br /><br />That said, if you don't have the earlier release, grab this one. Bergonzi, del Monaco, and Corelli were the three best Ernani performers of the 20th century and you can hear why in the broadcasts available on several labels. Yes, I know Domingo and Pavarotti sang the role but neither of them come anywhere near these three. While Bergonzi may not be as high-voltage as Corelli or del Monaco, he has power enough as well as a beautiful tone. Schippers propels the score very well and the sining of all is first-rate as well as each making the roles their own. Leontyne Price was one of the greatest sopranos of any century and her powerful, richly burnished tones bring the role to life. She and Bergonzi recorded this opera for RCA but the live performance in fine sound is even more remarkable with its theatrical feel.<br /><br />Grab it while Sony is still releasing it.

0446691437|5.0|This book was originally recommended to me by an acquaintance after I expressed some exasperation with how to approach my own creativity. The brilliance of this book is that its approach to writer's block is not mundane or ordinary. In essence it builds up to explaining that what we create is not of our own doing but a reflection of a higher plane, or what I have always called a higher plateau. In other words, what you create already exists in the divine nature of the universe, you are merely the vessel by which it is revealed.  I once new a guy, back in high school, who looked at some of the art I did and he said it made him want to quit trying, himself. I asked him why and replied that he wasn't an artist and he could never make anything as good as what I had shown him. Well, this book conquers that notion because if creativity is just a reflection of a higher plateau then it means anyone can be creative if they learn for themselves how to tap into that higher place. That's a beautiful idea.  I have long felt that I have been naturally tapped into a river, of sorts, that flows through the universe and gives us glimpses into what is beyond the human perception of the physical world. In my opinion, that is the source of creativity and this book taps into that. Although the backdrop for the author is writing, this book is a short yet great read for anyone interested in creativity of any sort.  As you'll no doubt see there are some negative reviews, especially regarding the spiritual aspect of this book. All I have to ask of prospective readers is, who seems happier? The cynics who write those reviews, or the people who recognize the beauty of illumination?

B005EHILV4|5.0|I've been playing around with my new Behringer XENYX 302USB Mixer and so far my impressions are positive.  I was nervous about buying it because there were no reviews at all, so I opened the box carefully and took out only the 302, using my own cable and on-line documentation. That way, if I had to return it, packing it back up would be easy.  I use Audacity (with a single core, Pentium 4 PC running XP Pro) to record, and the program recognized the 302 (as USB codex), no problem.  One thing I wanted to do is record from an iPod Touch 4G to Audacity, then play that Audacity track back and record another track against it from the iPod. I used a mono cable that is 1/4 inch on one end (plugged into the mic jack of the 302) and 1/8 inch on the other (plugged into the headphone jack of the iPod).  I used an app called Chordbot to play a progression on the iPod, which was recorded through the 302 into Audacity. I didn't care that the track was mono, but if I wanted stereo, I could have used the line input on the 302 with RCA cables going to an 1/8th inch stereo plug.  Once my chord progression was recorded on an Audacity track, I played that back by using an RCAs to 1/8 inch plug to connect the line input on the 302 to the headphone jack of the computer. By pushing the red button on the 302, which selects input from the USB (the computer), and the black button next to it, which sends the signal to the headphones, I could hear the Audacity track playing as I recorded a new track, this time using an app called Thumbjams on the iPod.  It worked very well. No hiss or other unwanted noise present.  The 302 assumes (incorrectly, in my case) that I want to hear the mic input through the earphones as I'm recording. I don't. I never monitor myself when singing or playing guitar, but listen only to the backing track.  I got around this by using the pan slider on the 302, panning my live performance all the way to the right. I then removed the right earphone from my ear. I panned thesound coming from the computer all the way to the left. This way I could hear the backing track but not my voice in the headphones.  My Audio Technica AT2020 microphone recorded fine--with no hiss or noise--with the 302's gain set at 12 o'clock, the mic volume maxed, and the main mix volume at about 2 o'clock.  I could generate hiss with the AT2020 if I cranked the 302's gain and volume all the way up, but I can do that with most any mixing deck.  I could not get as loud a hissless track using the 2020 and the 302 as I would like. A preamp is probably called for. But the signal was usable if I increased the gain a bit in Audacity after recording, or if I doubled a track.  In addition to the iPod experiment, I recorded a nylon-string guitar, then recorded a vocal track against it. Used the AT2020 for both tracks. Worked fine.  I have an old Radio Shack dynamic mic with a built-in TSR cable that I tried. It also recorded well, for what it is. (I sound terminally depressed when I record with this mic, so only dig it out for experiments such as this.)  All in all, I'm liking the 302 and plan to use it instead of the XENYX 802/UCA202 USB interface rig I was using.  WOWSERS. Important update. The USB codec that Windows installed when I first plugged in the 302 doesn't play nice with Audacity. Often when I try to play back or play back and record, there is no sound through the 302, even though I can see audio levels in Audacity.  I went to the Behringer website and downloaded the ASIO 32 bit driver. Now things are great. Except. Whatever USB slot you install the driver to is taken over by the driver and can't used by any other audio codec.  This means that if you unplug the 302 and plug another audio device into the same slot, it can only play--if it will--using the Behringer ASIO codec. Other slots are unaffected. It's possible to undo this by running the setup file again and choosing to uninstall the driver.  I'm willing to give up a USB slot to the 302 because I'm liking it so much and will probably use it every day. YMMV.

0812992792|5.0|In The Orphan Master's Son Adam Johnson brings to life the concept and reality of North Korea as only a master could.  He knits together reality with one of the great fictions of movie history (Casablanca) but transcends even Rick's character with that of Jun Do, the orphan master's son.  Jun Do's character starts at the lowest rung in North Korea, an orphan, at least an orphan due to the denial by the orphan master to even acknowledge him as his son.  Jun Do's launch outside the orphanage starts with  carrying out clandestine missions for the State (as directed by the Dear Leader Kim Jong Il) where he shows promise in learning foreign languages, then moves to high adventure at sea where he rises to hero status only to fall from grace.  His subsequent incarceration exposes him to a camp where exhausted workers suffer their grisly terminal exploitation as unwilling blood and organ donors.  Then almost by accident he manages to transform himself to a new identity as the second most powerful person in North Korea, one regarded with paranoiac fear even by Kim Jong Il.  It is the last transition that allows Jun Do the pleasure of finding his Ilsa, the most beloved actress in all of North Korea for whom Kim Jong Il personally writes scripts and secretly loves.    Along Jun Do's winding trail, Johnson introduces a myriad of heterogeneous characters extending from two American women rowing around the world to North Korean fishermen pressed into service to sponsor spies and carry out absurd personal missions for the Dear Leader's whims.  Jun Do and his fellow cast members reveal a state that most of us can only imagine--one devoted entirely to Kim Jong Il and his obsessions, his world view, his total control of information, his complete disregard for common morality.  Fear permeates and dominates every person's single day, their every action, their every \\"private\\" conversation.    Johnson's lively writing uses diverse strokes to paint this wide ranging action to evoke both acceptance and rejection by his characters' anima. Using fascinating style and imagination, he weaves together so many emotions and conditions from despair to cautious hope to probe a culture with which few of us are at all familiar that his book deserves a read, maybe two to savor it fully.

B003ZSH606|5.0|Jamiroquai's career for the past twenty years has been a long and curious one. First starting out as offering one of the few funk/soul based musically genuinely based in live instrumental productions with heavy songcraft and arrangements,the band gradually shed members at the end of it's first decade and relied more on heavy production and dancibility. Their previous studio set [[ASIN:B000B5XZLU Dynamite]] was not 100% up to their standards. And a compilation released not long after only featured two new songs. Seemed Jamiroquai was over. Newer bands/soloists had arrived to fill the void they left. Taking several years between the last few album releases have given them a chance to figure out what kind of music they can deal best with. And that it might just be possible to extend on their peak period without looking embarrassing. Now Jay Kay has reuped with a new Jamiroquai band that's quite a bit larger and self contained than the original including bassist Paul Turner,guitarist Rob Harris,keyboardist Matt Johnson and original member Derrick McKensie on drums along with a horn section and backround singers.<br /><br />  On this album Jamiroquai have a sound that doesn't have much to do with the sound of their earlier recordings. And certainly not the previous two. While Jay's voicals,whether due to his hard living past or overeaching vocally over time,is continuing to lose the range and volume it once had the material here is unique and diverse. Sure the digeredoo sound is of course long gone. What is here is a sound that,overall blends Jamiroquai's funkier and more soulful influences with stronger elements of singer-songwriter and pop/rock. The upbeat title song and the pretty ballad \\"Blues Skies\\" are basically built around acoustic guitars.  \\"White Knuckle Ride\\" and \\"All Good In The Hood\\" are the kind of Rod Temperton/Steve Arrington influenced sophistifunk  Jamiroquai have always excelled with. Again,both have a somewhat subdued undertone even still. The arrangements of \\"Smoke And Mirrors\\",\\"She's A Fast Peruader\\" and \\"Hey Floyd\\" are a reminder of the type of polyrhythmic \\"united funk\\" style instrumental power they were always able to insert into their sound.<br /><br />  While \\"Hurtin\\" does,to an extend replicate the sound of \\"Virtual Insanity\\" a little other songs such as the mildly 70's light rock influenced \\"Lifeline\\",with it's almost Beatle like refrain as well as \\"Two Completely Different Things\\" and \\"Goodbye To My Dancer\\" return to the singer-songwriter type pop funk of the title song. It all rounds out with another smooth groove in \\"Never Gonna Be Another\\". Lyrically Jay is resolving a bit of sewing his wild oates with this album. Not only that but as much of a return to form in terms of live instrumentation it is,the production is rather subdued by Jamiroquai standards. In some ways it's a return to the form of their first four albums. On another end it actually represents a completely different group-a more understated and somewhat adult Jamiroquai.  Not sure if this is the end of the band,since they have signed to a new label or the start of a new beginning. Hope it's the latter. The band and their creative vision are more than worth it.Smoke And Mirrors\\",\\"She's A Fast Peruader\\" and \\"Hey Floyd\\" are a reminder of the type of polyrhythmic \\"united funk\\" style instrumental power they were always able to insert into their sound. B0036T32LQ|2.0|What's keeping me from giving this movie 1 star is the assumption that Christopher Smith's film is simply a drawn-out, exaggerated metaphor for a young mother who continually finds herself trapped by the cycle of abuse that passes from parent to child, from one generation to the next. It's great when a movie throws you more curves and plot twists than a single viewing can be used to comprehend; Memento, Shutter Island, Inception for a few examples. It's frustrating when a director gives you an open-ended disarray of contradictory plot movements and 'what the fu..' moments and then never bother to even attempt an explanation. You're just suppose to go with it, reason be damned. Well, that's just not good enough. B005K0HDGE|5.0|At first glance, 11/22/63 appears to be a relatively standard Stephen King journey. Strong characters enliven a world that becomes ever-darker as a man pushes to change the past. However, 11/22/63 is probably Stephen King's most mature book to date, one that doesn't veer into horror territory but instead focuses on questions of what implications there might be if we changed history, and more importantly, is a beautiful love story.  11/22/63, in a quick overview, is about Jake Epping, a teacher in Maine who is approached by the owner of the local diner with a proposition - go back in time and stop the Kennedy assassination and in doing so, hopefully stop Vietnam from happening, Martin Luther King, Jr. from being assassinated, and more. Though reluctant and unbelieving at first, Jake learns of the ability to go back in time through a warp in the man's diner, and takes on the challenging task of fighting against history that doesn't want to be changed. In the course of his years-long journey, Jake meets and falls in love with a beautiful, young librarian in a small town in Texas, and while he continues to track Lee Harvey Oswald and attempt to stop the assassination, he battles with his false identity in thepast, his mission, and his love for this woman.  The love story in 11/22/63 is beautifully carved out, and 11/22/63 was one of the only times I've had tears in my eyes reading a book. It is an excellent love story, an excellent thriller, and gives great nods to readers of King's other books such as \\"It\\" and \\"The Langoliers.\\"  It is one of his finest books, and that's saying something considering how diverse and incredible a catalog he has built up. I highly recommend to anyone interested in a great novel devoid of horror and filled with excitement and joy.

B0019N8P2W|4.0|MTV obviously made compromises to release this DVD set. As everyone knows, the original music is replaced by generic songs, and the 2 movies are the abbreviated versions that were designed to air as reruns on MTV. With that being said, I'm not going to argue whether or not MTV should have tried harder with this release. The fact is, it's a show that's been off the air for a decade that was never as mainstream as say, South Park, The Simpsons, or Family Guy. As fans we are lucky to finally have something of high quality, instead of the poor quality VHS rips or Censored-for-content \\"The N\\" versions that have been floating around on the internet for years.  The lack of the original music is disappointing - as someone who watched the originals when it was on MTV, and then watched the modified versions on this DVD set, I do notice the difference. The music did help pull the viewer in to a Late 90's/Early 2000's timeline. But, they honestly didn't do a horrible job with the replacement generic music, and new fans to the show would probably not even be aware of the change unless they did some research on the fan sites. As a compromise, go to a website like \\"Outpost Daria\\" and pull up the song lists from each episode and make a custom \\"Daria\\" playlist to listen to before or after watching the show.  With regards to the actual DVD release: The disc case seems a bit poorly made. The front plastic cover came a bit warped, causing the cover artwork to look distorted. Not a huge deal, because most of the time this is going to sit on the shelf wedged in between a bunch of other DVDs. The extra content is nice, although a bit minimal. It would have been nice to see more from the behind-the-scenes production of the show. But back in 1997 I doubt the staff even considered that some day people would be interested in seeing them work their day to day job on a bonus section of a video disc.  The only major problem I have with this release, is that the 2 movies are located on the last disc under extras. If you watch the series straight through, you will miss out on watching the movies in the proper order. The first movie, \\"Is it Fall Yet?\\" should be watched after the episode \\"Dye! Dye! My Darling.\\"  The last movie, \\"Is It College Yet?\\" should be watched after the last episode of the series, \\"Boxing Daria.\\" Even if they couldn't find a way around needing to squeeze the two movies on the last disc under extras, they should have at least included some type of note or warning for viewers who want to watch the series in order.  All in all, Daria was a great show that truly was unique, if not misunderstood by many. Despite the flaws of this DVD release, I feel that any fan of the show, whether new or old, should pick up a copy. And who knows - maybe in another ten years the music industry will have changed enough where the episodes with the original music can be re-released. I doubt MTV would pass up an opportunity to sell it to us again!

0439023521|3.0|This book has so many reviews, I didn't intend to write one. As it is, I'll skip the plot introduction and setup and go straight to my thoughts.<br /><br />Without a doubt, this book is a page-turner. Indeed, the same is true of the whole trilogy; I blew through all three books in a weekend. And it was a great ride. I liked Katniss well enough, and while I was reading I was certainly invested in the tale.<br /><br />In retrospect, though, this trilogy was compelling to me mostly because it's so fast-paced and action-driven. Not that that's the only thing it has going for it: Collins does a good job of developing the society, there are some intriguing plot elements and I liked the angle the book takes with the romance (in the first book, at least). And I liked that the book doesn't make out-of-place references to our current society or give infodumps on what happened between the modern day and its futuristic setting. But already, looking back on the trilogy I'm underwhelmed. So, a few of the problems:<br /><br />- The characterization is a bit iffy. I liked Katniss, but she didn't ever feel like a real teenager (except maybe in the third book). Peeta is sometimes sweet, but way too perfect. Gale seemed interesting, but we never saw much of him. The secondary characters aren't awful, but there just isn't much here that's memorable.<br /><br />- The premise seems specially created to give the characters serious moral dilemmas. Only, the book neatly avoids those dilemmas. The setup seems to require Katniss to kill basically nice people in order to survive.... the actual plot sidesteps that.<br /><br />- Speaking of the plot: a bit too gimmicky for my taste. I'd like less reliance on monsters and magical obstacle courses and such, and more conflict arising from the characters themselves. Your mileage may vary. The first book isn't too bad about this, but there's more and more of it as the trilogy continues.<br /><br />- And speaking of the setup. I simply never bought that forcing a couple dozen randomly-selected teenage (and younger) boys and girls to kill each other on national TV would be a good PR move for any government. Especially with all the efforts to humanize them--the pre-Games interviews, having viewers witness every moment of their struggles, strength and suffering, interviewing their families and friends, and so on. I bought that the Districts had to accept this because they were oppressed. I didn't buy the people in the Capitol thinking this was all good fun.<br /><br />- Finally, I could never figure out why, when there are so few people left in the world, they'd confine themselves to such small areas. District 12 only has 8000 people (the size of a small town) and seems to be the only settlement in all of Appalachia. So, why does everyone live within a fenced-in area as if this was a zombie book? Wild animals (the reason given in the book) didn't necessitate such a drastic response from either the Native Americans or the original European settlers, so I assumed it was a political ploy to keep the people under control.... but that didn't make a lot of sense either. With such abundant land and natural resources, why would the government want to keep the population small, starving and with little to lose when it could instead take credit for a growing population and improved standards of living as they made use of the surrounding area? And would controlling a wider area really be a problem for a government that already exercises such tight control over such vast distances? Presumably they're already capable of controlling it, or dissenters would just run off into the wilderness and create their own societies? This is simply never addressed.<br /><br />Anyway, this trilogy is entertaining enough, but if somebody asked me to recommend an exciting series about teenagers fighting a bad government, I'd recommend Marsden's Tomorrow series before I'd recommend this.nger) boys and girls to kill each other on national TV would be a good PR move for any government. I bought that the Districts had to accept this because they were oppressed. I didn't buy the people in the Capitol thinking this was all good fun.  - Finally, I could never figure out why, when there are so few people left in the world, they'd confine themselves to such small areas. And would controlling a wider area really be a problem for a government that already exercises such tight control over such vast distances? Presumably they're already capable of controlling it, or dissenters would just run off into the wilderness and create their own societies? This is simply never addressed.  Anyway, this trilogy is entertaining enough, but if somebody asked me to recommend an exciting series about teenagers fighting a bad government, I'd recommend Marsden's Tomorrow series before I'd recommend this.

0385535139|5.0|What do you get when you cross a young, burned-out, corporate lawyer with two ham and egg, ambulance chasing, bickering street lawyers?  The result is John Grisham's thoroughly entertaining legal thriller, The Litigators.  The Litigators doesn't quite have the seriousness of purpose as The Pelican Brief or The Firm.  Still, this book deals with some serious issues and imparts some important lessons.<br /><br />David Zinc is a young, high-priced lawyer from one of Chicago's prestige firms, Rogan Rothberg.  Going to work one day, Zinc has a meltdown and when he arrives at his firm's lobby, he's seen diving head-first back into the elevator.  After spending all day drinking, he ends up directing a cab driver to an address he sees on an advertisement, the law firm of Finley and Figg.  Oscar Finley and Wally Figg are barely scratching out a living chasing ambulances and handling no fault divorces and DUIs.  Finley \\"was still married to his first wife, a terrifying woman he wanted to sue every day for his own divorce.  But he couldn't afford it.  After thirty-two years of lawyering, Oscar Finley couldn't afford much of anything.\\"  The younger Wally Figg struggles with alcoholism, has been divorced 4 times, and has more than a few DUIs under his belt.  Both lawyers took three tries to pass the bar.  The Harvard-educated Zinc begs for a job, and they offer him one at a ridiculously low salary.<br /><br />Figg has big dreams of a tort lawsuit with a big payout.  The firm gets a chance when one of his clients dies and his family claims his death was caused by the cholesterol drug, Krayoxx.  Figg files a $100 million lawsuit against the third largest pharmaceutical company, Varrick.  Yet the firm has never filed in federal court and has never appeared before a jury trial.  Varrick sees the Chicago-case as a weak link, and they decide to test the waters by going to trial against Finley and Figg.  The lawyers are so out of their league that it is a hoot, but Zinc tries to bring some sanity to this insane situation.<br /><br />The Litigators is funny, but there are some lessons to be learned here.  When something is too good to be true, it usually is and that it's possible to be too greedy.  Also, that despite good efforts, it's not always possible to change people--as Zinc tries to bring positive change to Finley and Figg.  We also learn that not all companies are sleazy and that some do own up to the damages caused by their product. You will also fall in love with unlikely hero, David Zinc, who learns more working for Finley and Figg than he ever did at Harvard Law.<br /><br />John Grisham is one of our best storytellers, and The Litigators will not disappoint.insane situation. B005J6LKVI|5.0|The Help in its idea alone is perhaps one of the most original ideas to come along in recent film history. I mean to say, a movie based on the hardships and life of African-American female housemaids during the 1960s? Not only that, but their Caucasian house bosses and all the social borders, stigmas, prejadices and love that intermix. The Help stars a stellar cast who some by no surprise are up for 2011 Oscar nominations, not to also mention the film's Oscar nomination for Best Picture of the Year. A very well-deserved achievement.  The film takes us into a fairly well off suburban neighborhood during the 1960s, when the first few ripples of the civil rights movement was beginning, and how it affected the always strict relationship that these Caucasian homeowners had with their maids. The film stars the up and coming Emma Stone as Skeeter, the single, headstrong, and brave writer who is on a mission to write a book detailing all the stories of the African-American maids around the neighborhood, to create a piece from their own point of view. This of course causes much controversy as not only are the maids hesitant to take part, as doing so may cause them to get into heaps of trouble, as well as risk their ability to ever be hired again, but also frightens her Caucasion relatives and friends, as writing such a book would risk bringing a dramatic change to their comfortable and stable domineering relationship with their housemaids. Viola Davis and Octavian Spencer play 2 other housemaids with their own house bosses - the spoiled, trite and cruel 'Hilly' played by Bryce Dallas Howard and 'Celia' played entertainingly and adorably well as the bubbly and joyful yet strong new-girl-on-the-block by Jessica Chastain. Viola and Octavian put on Oscar-nominated performances and truly steal the show, bringing us humor, compassion and stellar wit to their characters. Their Oscar nominations are extremely well-deserved. Veteran actress Allison Janney plays the insecure and emotionally struggling mother of Skeeter, who is most on the fence about her firing of her oldest housemaid, struggling with her love and compassion vs. her social status.  The film brings shows us all the troubles and tribulations of the housemaids (there are others besides Viola and Octavia in more minor roles with their own homeowners played well by other supporting cast members), but not only that, the film also displays the tension between the Caucasian homeowners themselves, thus showing us that even though they are at a socially sigmatic position as the white \\"slave-drivers,\\" they do not embrace such a status, yet struggle to show as much compassion to their housemaids meanwhile maintaining the authority society tells them they must have.  Our star, Skeer (Emma Stone) encounters tension from both sides, as well as from her mother who can't stand to see her single anymore. She eventually begins her work with writing her book and things flair up from there.  What makes this such an incredible film is its love for the characters. Dialogue throughout is extremely precise in terms of dialect and tone, not to also mention interesting and very well written. The amazing performances only highlight this aspect, and we grow to love the characters through all their struggles. The most vital being 2 in particular - Skeeter's frustration with her family as the firing of their oldest maid to her is akin to the firing of her own mother (as the housemaid for the most part RAISED Skeeter herself), and Aibileen's (Viola Davis) struggles with overcoming the death of her son and all the scars that has left her in terms of virtually all Caucasians; she walks the line between humility and deeply embedded anger, meanwhile always walking in a state of ongoing sadness.  The drama with the homeowner side of things eventually grows as more of the comedic relief throughout the film, but the audience will be much more interested in how the housemaids overcome their side of things. If there was any flaw, I felt that towards the end, while the struggles with the White homeowner's relationships build to be more entertaining and not so much heartfelt, things felt a bit forced by the end, yet it never goes so far as to step over the line of unbelievability.  The pacing and editing in the film is spot-on, and even with a running time of 2 hours and 20 minutes, you'll feel the need to watch this one again and again, simply because the setting, pacing and dialogue in the film is simply either too entertaining, passionate and soothing as a whole.  Lastly, for all the guys out there worried about their girlfriends or wives dragging them to see this one, please keep in mind that this is NOT a \\"Chick Flick.\\" Far from it. No, this is a realistic fiction (although based on the author's true life story) film about the struggles of people trying to live through an era where they were being both pushed down, intimidated, yet freed from years and years of segregation. Instead of this being a film displaying the civil rights movement as a whole (as in the film Malcom X), this scopes in on one suburban neighborhood, showing us what everyday people did to deal with the societal changes, and all the inner struggles as they now had to find a line between tradition and societal progression.  Overall a fantastic, heartwarming, gritty, and truely moving film.

Author Marissa Meyer has done a marvelous job of creating a truly original story inside the trappings of a classic fairytale. B00007KWHP|5.0|Hearing this album always brings me back. My brother had this album when I was a kid and he'd play it every morning when I was a 6-year-old getting ready for school. It was the beginning of what remains my personal favorite lineup of Yes- Jon Anderson's unique vocals and spiritual lyrics, Chris Squire's melodious and loud bass (not to mention his harmonies were a great match for Anderson), Steve Howe's versatile guitar work, Bill Bruford's jazz-flavored drums and then-newcomer Rick Wakeman's incredible keyboard orchestra. It was also the debut of Roger Dean's artwork with Yes. He designed a ready-to-fall-apart planet on the cover and some cool paintings which would grace the photo book. Some of the classic rock stations here in the USA just aired an episode of In The Studio With Redbeard, which featured this classic. And of course, one of my favorite scenes in School Of Rock is that where the father of one child holds up a CD copy of Fragile and asks \\"How is this music supposed to help my son?\\" Read on and you may understand.<br /><br />It all begins with one of Yes' 1st big hits \\"Roundabout,\\" an 8-minute tour de force, with features Steve's classical guitar work and the lyrics speak of a trip Yes took in a car through Scotland with roundabouts and mountains that came out of the sky. Next is the 1st of the \\"personal ideas\\" quilogy- Rick's \\"Cans And Brahms,\\" a short but sweet take on the 3rd movement of Brahms' 4th and final symphony. This has my vote as the most innovative of the \\"personal ideas\\"- one friend of mine said he was playing this and his father (no fan of rock music) found it interesting. Following it is Jon Anderson's \\"We Have Heaven\\"- the most fun of the \\"personal ideas.\\" Jon uses several vocal tracks singing \\"Tell the moondog, tell the march hare\\" (whatever that means) and then sings in high tenor \\"We have heaven\\" and later \\"Yes, he's here\\" (the moondog or the march hare?) and a few other things until a door slams on Jon's multi-choir piece and you canhear someone walking away. \\"South Side Of The Sky\\" speaks of an excursion in Antarctica \\"Were we ever colder on that day, a million miles away.\\" Wakeman has an exquisite piano solo in the middle. Getting to side 2 of Fragile (on the LP, that is), Bill does a brief 16 bar track \\"5% For Nothing,\\" supposedly a tongue in cheek jab at the negotiations set up, so this has my vote as the most sarcastic of the \\"personal ideas.\\" The music sounds like something you'd hear right before a commercial break in a talk show. Next is Jon's spiritual \\"Long Distance Runaround\\" with a lengthy jam session between Rick and Steve and Chris and Bill join in. Chris' \\"The Fish\\" segues into it, where Chris adds a number of bass tones and plays his instrument like a lead guitar, the most popular of the \\"personal ideas\\" since it gets the most airplay. And don't ask me what \\"Schindeleria Praemataurus\\" means. Steve has the final and most exquisite \\"personal idea\\" with a classical guitar piece called \\"Mood For A Day.\\" It inspired me to learn it on guitar. Concluding Fragile (well, almost...) is a mindblowing finale \\"Heart Of The Sunrise,\\" Jon's ode to the environment. There is some fine duelling between Chris and Bill (with Rick and Steve later joining in, think the opposite of the mini-jam session in \\"Long Distance Runaround\\") at the intro before Jon's voice mixes between soft and attention grabbing. \\"Love comes to you and you follow. Lose one onto the heart of the sunrise. Sharp distance.\\" Then as the final notes chime (after 10.5 minutes of jumping between G sharp minor and B flat minor), it ends fast and furious. Don't get up and change the record (or CD or tape) just yet. Listen for a reprise of Jon's \\"We Have Heaven.\\"<br /><br />So there you have it- 5 solo pieces and 4 tracks of pure musical teamwork that has hardly ever been repeated in musical history.

The most shocking is a frail Mercury, in pain, standing up, for the \\"These Are the Days of Our Lives\\" video. The on-the-set color footage, showing Mercury waiting for the camera to start, is haunting. His sharp jawline (from AIDS) looks like it could cut through steel. Mercury's left eye is noticeably blood shot, and he looks plain ill, yet he pulled off one of his greatest on-screen performances for the music video.  It's nice to see the black-and-white film footage of Queen actually recording part of their \\"News of the World\\" album in 1977, and the 1976 live Hyde Park footage, although shown only in a couple too-brief segments, is magnificent. Footage of Queen's 1977 tour also is examined, through footage that wonderfully blends old videotape footage with film footage of the same gig.  I also learned of Roger Taylor's hatred for the \\"Hot Space\\" songs that sported dance-like beats, and how Queen almost broke up in 1982/83.  One of rock's greatest mysteries, though, has to be a now-missing-in-action John Deacon, Queen's bassist, who, for some reason, refused to take part in this documentary, as he has in all things Queen-related over the last several years. Is Deacon still alive? Anyone seen or heard from him? Supposedly Deacon gave May and Taylor his blessing to carry on with the Queen legacy, yet there's no word at all from Deacon. Wasthere any bad blood? Taylor was quoted a few years ago saying something like \\"You'll have to ask John about that, and I don't think he's in the right place to talk about that now.\\" Maybe a bit of bad blood exists on John's part?
