B003EYVXXW|4.0|The film depicts Roman Egypt in late antiquity and tries to tackle all of the most important developments in that era: the collapse of decadent Pagan society, the growing and unsustainable inequality between the rich and poor, the rise of Christianity, the rejection of religious pluralism, the decay of the Roman Empire, and the decline of Greco-Roman science and learning. Obviously it would be a miracle that any 2 hour film could tackle so many topics succesfully without employing cheesy dialogue so I knew this film would be cheesy before I watched it and it certainly was.  On the plus side the film does an incredible job of depicting the various competing factions in a fair light. Both the Christians and the Pagans are depicted with their merits and flaws. The viewer gets a real glympse of how so many people became attracted to Christianity amongst the back-drop of the decadent Pagan society. The Christians are shown as just as zealous in their destruction of learning and science as they are in ridding the city of hunger and disease, whilst the Pagans are shown as obsessed with pursuing pleasure of the body and mind and having no regard for the poor or their slaves.  The film is incredibly careful with facts which is quite rare in the genre of historical epics. It is careful in that it does not show St. Cyril as directly responsible for the murder of Hypatia though a connection can be inferred. It also clearly explains that Hypatia's writings are lost so that we can only speculate on what exactly she wrote about. Every scene has been carefully weighed to insure historical accuracy for the sacrifice of entertainment. Thus there is a scene in the film where Hypatia's father discusses his daughter with other elder men as not a typical \\"woman\\" who will never marry a man and lead the normal life of a woman. The only reason this scene is included in the film is to insure that the viewer is not led into thinking that Pagan society was inclusive of women in the academic field and that Hypatia was the exception rather than the rule. The scene is educational but does nothing to add to it's entertainment value.  In summary the film is incredibly cheesy and not very entertaining but as an educational tool it gets 5 stars. I would recommend it to any teacher or parent for shedding light on an era all too often ignored by both Hollywood and the Western school system. To anybody who has never heard of Hypatia or has little knowledge of how and why Paganism was replaced by Christianity this film is also a great launching pad for further research.

B006P0FD4W|4.0|First off, I should say that I LOVED parts one and two. The first two relied more heavily on very slow-building tension. These predecessors basically \\"taught\\" viewers how to watch these movies in the first 20-30 minutes by offering numerous subtle, relatively unimportant objects moving as if a spectral breeze had shifted them. This way when such production devices became important, the viewer had a trained eye--not unlike what was done with White Noise. These movies convey a style that is very unusual. So it came as no surprise to me that there was little middle ground in people's opinions of them; they loved'em or hated'em. I love'em. Why? Because my senses are all on full power; I'm all in; I'm practically concentrating on the screen and listening to every creak trying to sleuth out the next clue that something fishy is going on in that house. Some people may call this \\"work\\". I call it cool. [But people chatting during the movie are a much greater distraction than normal under the circumstances.]<br /><br />This third installment was my least favorite, but I can totally understand why it may be others' favorite. While it still employed subtle moving objects, it did it less, instead relying on more mainstream devices to provoke scared jumps from the audience. It also borrowed more heavily from the Poltergeist movies than the first two--not that I minded. The characters' investigation into the strange goings-on was more methodical and plot-driven. The first two were more event-driven and investigated more out of fear and curiosity. The differences between 3 and 1 & 2 were subtle, but numerous, chief amongst them being that \\"the paranormal\\" functions as a character in this movie, rather than a mysterious \\"force\\" in the first two. As such, the actions of \\"the paranormal\\" were more blatant and felt more like \\"it\\" was doing something \\"to someone\\" whereas in 1 & 2 it was more like \\"something was happening\\" to someone in a haunted house.<br /><br />The plot is simple. A family lives in a house. Weird things start happening. Step-dad starts putting cameras around the house. Things get weirder. And from there anything more would give too much away. But while the first two movies' endings left us largely to wild speculation, I will say that this one ends with something of an explanation of the paranormal activity.<br /><br />It doesn't really matter in which order you watch these movies. However, each sequel (or in this case prequel) was designed to mold over the events of the previous installment. So watch them in order if it's convenient. I also demand you watch these with the lights off. It makes it easier to avoid distractions while you're concentrating on the screen.use. Weird things start happening. Even though the scenario is familiar and people might be thinking \\"ID4\\" this movie is focused on being more compact.  It follows one man (Sergeant Michael Nantz played by Aaron Eckhart) and one platoon over the course of a day as they make their way through LA with initial confidence in order to rescue stranded civilians and, with each seeming alien encounter, their confidence is eroded as the aliens demonstrate that they are adapting their military strategies; at first they are just a ground force coming out of the ocean but soon they have air support and then unmanned drones via a central broadcasting hub.  These bugs adapt.  And this is what makes this grimy, compact movie more interesting.  This could be a metaphor for a new virus attacking populations; it could be a metaphor for a well-planned war against governments; or it could just be any invading force that is going to give us a run for our money.  The military is played straight and makes our fighting men and women (though vulnerable and being pushed back in the film) look intelligent and sympathetic.  The film doesn't try to make any grand statements about anything really; you can take it for what it is or sprinkle in your own interpretations. B0068RGVMK|3.0|Tuomas reached for the stars on this one but bit off a little more than he can chew, this is part epic, part epic fail. Let's start with the vocals before I address the musical compostitions. As far as the Tarja/Annette camp rivalry goes, having seen them live 3X , twice with Tarja once with Annette, I can say unequivocally that Tarja blows Annette away on EVERY level: technical talent,vocal tone, emotiveness,range, stage presence and just plain good looks, Tarja sounds EXACTLY as good live as on CD, whereas Annette sounded like a shrieky whiner that could barely sing her own songs live and outright butchered the older material. Annette comes across as a phony in every way, including her name which is also fake, the 40 yr old mother of 2 with naturally straight short blonde hair and the body of a 12 yr old Philipino boy looks outright ridiculous in her \\"Goth Girl\\" outfit.  The real problem is that her vocals are now the limiting factor of the band and aren't up to par with the above average musicianship and songwriting of the rest of the band, while I found them at least tolerable on this release and not as much of a distraction as on Dark Passion Play, you can hear that they were heavily layered, or layered with Marco's vocals to overcome the shortcomings and Tuomas really squeezed everything out of her he can get, her average \\"one-dimensional\\" voice is about as good as it's going to get here, no room for growth.  Now onto the music: they have gone as full blown symphonic pop/goth metal soundtrack sounding as they could possibly get on this release, some of it works well some doesn't, the first half of the album starts off strong , if a bit schizophrenic,strangely starting with a Finnish lullabye then onto the catchy single \\"storytime\\"  followed by the decent \\"ghost river\\" the strange jazzy ballad \\" slow, love slow\\" though it works well, then the Celtic sounding uptempo \\"I want my tears back\\" followed by one of the two best tracks on the album \\"Scaretale\\" a heavy unique Tim Burton inspired number, then the very enjoyable middle eastern instrumental \\"Arabesque\\" , unfortunately the album completely loses steam in the second half and it becomes one intolerable bore of mediocre slow to mid tempo numbers , with the one exception \\"Last Ride of the Day\\" a very catchy uptempo and uplifting number that is my favorite track on the album. The last real song on the album \\"Song of Myself\\" should really be titled \\" Victim of Itself\\" because that's what it really is and this is really Tuomas's biggest mistake on the album, the song starts off very strong and promising then devolves into a nearly 8 minute narration that renders this song virtually unlistenable for repeat playings, there should have been two versions of this song, an edited album version that does away with the narrations and the \\"special edition\\" movie version that includes them.  The album basically ends on a whimper after the boring narration there is the instrumental medley \\"Imaginaerum\\" and that's it.  If this album had the proper editing of the boring parts, a few more catchy heavy numbers and a few less slow/mid-tempo numbers, it would have been 4 stars, and the addition of a proper female lead that can push vocal boundaries would have gotten it to 5 stars.  If these guys really want to progress from here they need to mesh this new highly produced symphonic sound with the heavyness and metal sensibilities of the \\"Wishmaster\\" album and either bring Tarja back into the fold or hire another stellar female vocalist, I would suggest Floor Jansen, the best and most underrated female vocalist in the biz right now and the only one with the vocal chops to take this band to new heights.
